<p><b>Brazil</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bc/En-us-Brazil.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Brazil.ogg" title="File:En-us-Brazil.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Brasil</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[bɾaˈziw]</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>), officially the <b>Federative Republic of Brazil</b> (Portuguese: <span lang="pt"><i>República Federativa do Brasil</i></span>, <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Pt-br-Rep%C3%BAblica_Federativa_do_Brasil.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/Pt-br-Rep%C3%BAblica_Federativa_do_Brasil.ogg" class="internal" title="Pt-br-República Federativa do Brasil.ogg">listen</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Pt-br-Rep%C3%BAblica_Federativa_do_Brasil.ogg" title="File:Pt-br-República Federativa do Brasil.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span><sup id="cite_ref-Bello1966v_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bello1966v-12">[12]</a></sup>), is the largest country in both <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>. As the world's fifth-largest country by both <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">area</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">population</a>, it is the largest country to have <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> as an <a href="/wiki/List_of_territorial_entities_where_Portuguese_is_an_official_language" title="List of territorial entities where Portuguese is an official language">official language</a> and the only one in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Philander2012_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philander2012-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CrocittiVallance2011_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrocittiVallance2011-14">[14]</a></sup> Bounded by the Atlantic Ocean on the east, Brazil has a <a href="/wiki/Coastline_of_Brazil" title="Coastline of Brazil">coastline</a> of 7,491 kilometers (4,655&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Geo_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Geo-15">[15]</a></sup> It borders all other South American countries except Ecuador and Chile and covers 47.3% of the continent's land area.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon River basin">Amazon River basin</a> includes a <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">vast tropical forest</a>, home to diverse <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">wildlife</a>, a variety of <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Brazil" title="Environment of Brazil">ecological systems</a>, and extensive natural resources spanning numerous <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Brazil" title="Protected areas of Brazil">protected habitats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Geo_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Geo-15">[15]</a></sup> This unique environmental heritage makes Brazil one of 17 <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a>, and is the subject of significant global interest and debate regarding deforestation and environmental protection.</p>
<p>Brazil was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous Brazilian">numerous tribal nations</a> prior to the landing in 1500 of explorer <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a>, who claimed the area for the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>. Brazil remained a <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Portuguese colony</a> until 1808, when the capital of the empire was <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">transferred from Lisbon to Rio de Janeiro</a>. In 1815, the colony was elevated to the rank of kingdom upon the formation of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a>. <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Independence">Independence</a> was achieved in 1822 with the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>, a unitary state governed under a constitutional monarchy and a parliamentary system. The ratification of the first constitution in 1824 led to the formation of a bicameral legislature, now called the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress</a>. The country <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_Republic_(Brazil)" title="Proclamation of the Republic (Brazil)">became a presidential republic</a> in 1889 following a military <i>coup d'état</i>. An authoritarian <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_military_dictatorship" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian military dictatorship">military junta</a> came to power <a href="/wiki/1964_Brazilian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1964 Brazilian coup d'état">in 1964</a> and ruled until 1985, after which civilian governance resumed. Brazil's current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">constitution</a>, formulated in 1988, defines it as a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The federation is composed of the union of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_District_(Brazil)" title="Federal District (Brazil)">Federal District</a>, the 26 <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">states</a>, and the 5,570 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Brazil" title="Municipalities of Brazil">municipalities</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Brazil's economy</a> is the world's ninth-<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">largest by nominal GDP</a> and seventh-<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">largest by GDP (PPP)</a> as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brazil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF.2C_October_2015_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF.2C_October_2015-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> A member of the <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a> group, Brazil until 2010 had one of the world's fastest growing major economies, with its economic reforms giving the country new international recognition and influence.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Brazil's <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Development_Bank" title="Brazilian Development Bank">national development bank</a> plays an important role for the country's economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Brazil is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G20</a>, <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Unasul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">CPLP</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a>. Brazil is a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> in Latin America and a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> in international affairs,<sup id="cite_ref-Seelke2010_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seelke2010-22">[22]</a></sup> with some analysts identifying it as an <a href="/wiki/Emerging_power" title="Emerging power">emerging global power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DominguezKim2013_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DominguezKim2013-23">[23]</a></sup> One of the world's major <a href="/wiki/Breadbasket" title="Breadbasket">breadbaskets</a>, Brazil has been the largest <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Brazil" title="Coffee production in Brazil">producer of coffee</a> for the last 150 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Neilson102_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neilson102-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Government_and_politics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Government and politics</span></a>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Brazil" title="Name of Brazil">Name of Brazil</a></div>
<p>It is likely that the word "Brazil" comes from the Portuguese word for <a href="/wiki/Caesalpinia_echinata" class="mw-redirect" title="Caesalpinia echinata">brazilwood</a>, a tree that once grew plentifully along the Brazilian coast.<sup id="cite_ref-Fausto1999_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fausto1999-25">[25]</a></sup> In Portuguese, brazilwood is called <i>pau-brasil</i>, with the word <i>brasil</i> commonly given the etymology "red like an ember", formed from Latin <i>brasa</i> ("ember") and the suffix <i>-il</i> (from <i>-iculum</i> or <i>-ilium</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Vincent2003_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent2003-26">[26]</a></sup> As brazilwood produces a deep red dye, it was highly valued by the European cloth industry and was the earliest commercially exploited product from Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker2007_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker2007-27">[27]</a></sup> Throughout the 16th century, massive amounts of brazilwood were harvested by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">indigenous peoples</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Tupi_people" title="Tupi people">Tupi</a>) along the Brazilian coast, who sold the timber to European traders (mostly Portuguese, but also French) in return for assorted European consumer goods.<sup id="cite_ref-Lee2011_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lee2011-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The official Portuguese name of the land, in original Portuguese records, was the "Land of the Holy Cross" (<i>Terra da Santa Cruz</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-Corporation1880_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corporation1880-29">[29]</a></sup> but European sailors and merchants commonly called it simply the "Land of Brazil" (<i>Terra do Brasil</i>) on account of the brazilwood trade.<sup id="cite_ref-L.C3.A9ry1990_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L.C3.A9ry1990-30">[30]</a></sup> The popular appellation eclipsed and eventually supplanted the official Portuguese name. Early sailors sometimes also called it the "Land of Parrots" (<i>Terra di Papaga</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Sokolow2003_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sokolow2003-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani language</a>, an official language of <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, Brazil is called "Pindorama". This was the name the indigenous population gave to the region, meaning "land of the palm trees".<sup id="cite_ref-Herrera-Sobek2012_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herrera-Sobek2012-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil" title="History of Brazil">History of Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Brazilian_history" title="Timeline of Brazilian history">Timeline of Brazilian history</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Cabraline_era">Pre-Cabraline era</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil#Precolonial_history" title="History of Brazil">History of Brazil §&#160;Precolonial history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cromlech.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Cromlech.jpg/220px-Cromlech.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Cromlech.jpg/330px-Cromlech.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/09/Cromlech.jpg 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="269" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cromlech.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Megalith" title="Megalith">Megaliths</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Stonehenge" title="Amazon Stonehenge">Solstice Archaeological Park</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Amap%C3%A1" title="Amapá">Amapá</a>, erected between 500 and 2000 years ago, probably to carry out <a href="/wiki/Astronomical" class="mw-redirect" title="Astronomical">astronomical</a> observations.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The earliest human remains found in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luzia_Woman" title="Luzia Woman">Luzia Woman</a>, were found in the area of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Leopoldo" title="Pedro Leopoldo">Pedro Leopoldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> and provide evidence of human habitation going back at least 11,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LevineCrocitti1999_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LevineCrocitti1999-34">[34]</a></sup> The earliest <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a> ever found in the Western Hemisphere was excavated in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">Amazon basin</a> of Brazil and <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">radiocarbon dated</a> to 8,000 years ago (6000 BC). The pottery was found near <a href="/wiki/Santar%C3%A9m,_Par%C3%A1" title="Santarém, Pará">Santarém</a> and provides evidence that the tropical forest region supported a complex prehistoric culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Eighth_Millennium_Pottery_from_a_Prehistoric_Shell_Midden_in_the_Brazilian_Amazon_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eighth_Millennium_Pottery_from_a_Prehistoric_Shell_Midden_in_the_Brazilian_Amazon-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Around the time of the Portuguese arrival, the territory of current day Brazil had an estimated indigenous population of 7 million people,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> mostly semi-nomadic who subsisted on hunting, fishing, gathering, and migrant agriculture. The indigenous population of Brazil comprised several large indigenous ethnic groups (e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Tup%C3%AD_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupí people">Tupis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guaranis</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%AA_peoples" title="Gê peoples">Gês</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawaks</a>). The Tupí people were subdivided into the <a href="/wiki/Tupiniquim_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupiniquim people">Tupiniquins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tupinamb%C3%A1_people" title="Tupinambá people">Tupinambás</a>, and there were also many subdivisions of the other groups.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the arrival of Europeans, the boundaries between these groups and their subgroups were marked by wars that arose from differences in culture, language and moral beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> These wars also involved large-scale military actions on land and water, with <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" title="Cannibalism">cannibalistic</a> rituals on <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> While heredity had some weight, leadership status was more subdued over time, than allocated in succession ceremonies and conventions.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> among the Indians had a different meaning than it had for Europeans, since it originated from a diverse socio-economic organization, in which asymmetries were translated into <a href="/wiki/Kinship" title="Kinship">kinship</a> relations.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_colonization">Portuguese colonization</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Colonial Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_(1865%E2%80%931939).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg/220px-Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg/330px-Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg/440px-Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_%281865%E2%80%931939%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2775" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Desembarque_de_Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral_em_Porto_Seguro_em_1500_by_Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_(1865%E2%80%931939).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Representation of the landing of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Porto_Seguro" title="Porto Seguro">Porto Seguro</a>, 1500.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The land now called Brazil was claimed for the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> on 22 April 1500, with the arrival of the Portuguese fleet commanded by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Boxer.2C_p._98_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer.2C_p._98-43">[43]</a></sup> The Portuguese encountered indigenous peoples divided into several tribes, most of whom spoke languages of the <a href="/wiki/Tupi%E2%80%93Guarani" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupi–Guarani">Tupi–Guarani</a> family, and fought among themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0100_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0100-44">[44]</a></sup> Though the first settlement was founded in 1532, colonization was effectively begun in 1534, when King <a href="/wiki/Dom_(title)" title="Dom (title)">Dom</a> <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">João&#160;III</a> of Portugal divided the territory into the fifteen private and autonomous <a href="/wiki/Captaincies_of_Brazil" title="Captaincies of Brazil">Captaincy Colonies of Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skidmore.2C_p..C2.A027_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skidmore.2C_p..C2.A027-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, the decentralized and unorganized tendencies of the captaincy colonies proved problematic, and in 1549 the Portuguese king restructured them into the <a href="/wiki/Governorate_General_of_Brazil" title="Governorate General of Brazil">Governorate General of Brazil</a>, a single and centralized Portuguese colony in South America.<sup id="cite_ref-Skidmore.2C_p..C2.A027_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skidmore.2C_p..C2.A027-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In the first two centuries of colonization, Indigenous and European groups lived in constant war, establishing <a href="/wiki/Opportunistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Opportunistic">opportunistic</a> alliances in order to gain advantages against each other.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> By the mid-16th century, <a href="/wiki/Sugar#Sugarcane" title="Sugar">cane sugar</a> had become Brazil's most important exportation product,<sup id="cite_ref-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0100_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0100-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and slaves purchased in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa#Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Slavery in Africa">slave market of Western Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> (not only those from Portuguese allies of their colonies in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mozambique" title="Portuguese Mozambique">Mozambique</a>), had become its largest import,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> to cope with <a href="/wiki/Plantation_economy" title="Plantation economy">plantations</a> of sugarcane, due to increasing international demand for Brazilian sugar.<sup id="cite_ref-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0102_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0102-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes,_1914.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes%2C_1914.jpg/220px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes%2C_1914.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes%2C_1914.jpg/330px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes%2C_1914.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes%2C_1914.jpg/440px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes%2C_1914.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="314" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B4nio_Parreiras_-_Pris%C3%A3o_de_Tiradentes,_1914.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Painting showing the arrest of <a href="/wiki/Tiradentes" title="Tiradentes">Tiradentes</a>; he was sentenced to death for his involvement in the best known <a href="/wiki/Inconfid%C3%AAncia_Mineira" title="Inconfidência Mineira">movement for independence</a> in Colonial Brazil.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the end of the 17th century, sugarcane exports began to decline,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and the discovery of gold by <a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">bandeirantes</a> in the 1690s would become the new backbone of the colony's economy, fostering a <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Gold_Rush" title="Brazilian Gold Rush">Brazilian Gold Rush</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> which attracted thousands of new <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">settlers</a> to Brazil from Portugal and all Portuguese colonies around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> This increased level of immigration in turn caused <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Emboabas" title="War of the Emboabas">some conflicts</a> between newcomers and old settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Portuguese expeditions known as <a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">Bandeiras</a> gradually advanced the Portugal colonial <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">original frontiers</a> in South America to approximately the current Brazilian borders.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In this era other European powers tried to colonize parts of Brazil, in incursions that the Portuguese had to fight, notably the French <a href="/wiki/France_Antarctique" title="France Antarctique">in Rio during the 1560s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equinoctial_France" title="Equinoctial France">in Maranhão during the 1610s</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Dutch in Bahia and Pernambuco</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Dutch%E2%80%93Portuguese_War" title="Dutch–Portuguese War">Dutch–Portuguese War</a>, after the end of <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Portuguese colonial administration in Brazil had two objectives that would ensure colonial order and the <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly</a> of Portugal's wealthiest and largest colony: to keep under control and eradicate all forms of <a href="/wiki/Slave_rebellion" title="Slave rebellion">slave rebellion</a> and resistance, such as the <a href="/wiki/Palmares_(quilombo)" title="Palmares (quilombo)">Quilombo of Palmares</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and to repress all movements for <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">autonomy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Inconfid%C3%AAncia_Mineira" title="Inconfidência Mineira">Minas Conspiracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom_with_Portugal">United Kingdom with Portugal</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg/260px-Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg" width="260" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg/390px-Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg/520px-Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1408" data-file-height="836" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_do_rei_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_VI_no_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Acclamation of <a href="/wiki/John_VI_of_Portugal" title="John VI of Portugal">King João VI</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, 6 February 1818</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In late 1807, Spanish and Napoleonic forces threatened the security of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Portugal" title="Continental Portugal">continental Portugal</a>, causing <a href="/wiki/John_VI_of_Portugal" title="John VI of Portugal">Prince Regent João</a>, in the name of <a href="/wiki/Maria_I_of_Portugal" title="Maria I of Portugal">Queen Maria I</a>, to move the royal court from <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0213_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boxer.2C_p..C2.A0213-67">[67]</a></sup> There they established some of Brazil's first financial institutions, such as its local <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchanges</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and its <a href="/wiki/Banco_do_Brasil" title="Banco do Brasil">National Bank</a>, additionally ending the Portuguese monopoly on Brazilian trade and opening Brazil to other nations. In 1809, in retaliation for being forced into exile, the Prince Regent ordered the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_conquest_of_French_Guiana" title="Portuguese conquest of French Guiana">Portuguese conquest of French Guiana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the end of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> in 1814, the courts of Europe demanded that Queen Maria I and Prince Regent João return to Portugal, deeming it unfit for the head of an ancient European monarchy to reside in a colony. In 1815, in order to justify continuing to live in Brazil, where the royal court had thrived for the past six years, the Crown established the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil,_and_the_Algarves" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil, and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil, and the Algarves</a>, thus creating a <a href="/wiki/Pluricontinental" class="mw-redirect" title="Pluricontinental">pluricontinental</a> transatlantic monarchic state.<sup id="cite_ref-Mosher2008_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mosher2008-70">[70]</a></sup> However, such a ploy didn't last long, since the leadership in Portugal resentful with the new status of its larger colony, continued to require the return of court to Lisbon (as postulated by the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Revolution_of_1820" title="Liberal Revolution of 1820">Liberal Revolution of 1820</a>), as well as groups of Brazilians, impatient for practical and real changes still demanded independence and a republic, as showed by the <a href="/wiki/Pernambucan_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Pernambucan Revolt">1817 Pernambucan Revolt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mosher2008_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mosher2008-70">[70]</a></sup> In 1821, as a demand of revolutionaries who had taken the city of <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Adelman2006_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adelman2006-71">[71]</a></sup> D. João VI was unable to hold out any longer, and departed for Lisbon. There he swore oath to the new constitution, leaving his son, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Prince Pedro de Alcântara</a>, as Regent of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Brazil" title="Kingdom of Brazil">Kingdom of Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_Empire">Independent Empire</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">Independence of Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg/260px-Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg" width="260" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg/390px-Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg/520px-Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2271" data-file-height="1268" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_of_Brazil_1888.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Declaration of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Independence_of_Brazil" title="War of Independence of Brazil">Brazilian independence</a> by Prince Pedro (later Emperor <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro&#160;I</a>) on 7 September 1822.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tensions between Portuguese and Brazilians increased, and the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cortes" title="Portuguese Cortes">Portuguese Cortes</a>, guided by the new political regime imposed by the 1820 Liberal Revolution, tried to re-establish Brazil as a colony.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The Brazilians refused to yield, and Prince Pedro decided to stand with them, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Declaration_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Declaration of Independence">declaring the country's independence from Portugal</a> on 7 September 1822.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> A month later, Prince Pedro was declared the first Emperor of Brazil, with the regnal title of Dom <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro&#160;I</a>, resulting in the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian War of Independence">Brazilian War of Independence</a>, which had already begun along this process, spread through northern, northeastern regions and in Cisplatina province.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> With the last Portuguese soldiers surrendering on 8 March 1824,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Portugal officially recognized Brazil on 29 August 1825.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><br />
On 7 April 1831, worn down by years of administrative turmoil and political dissensions with both liberal and conservative sides of politics, including an attempt of <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Equator" title="Confederation of the Equator">republican secession</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> as well as unreconciled with the way that absolutists in Portugal had given to the succession of King John VI, Pedro&#160;I went to Portugal to <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">reclaim his daughter's crown</a>, abdicating the Brazilian throne in favor of his five-year-old son and heir (who thus became the Empire's second monarch, with the regnal title of Dom <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro&#160;II</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg/170px-Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg" width="170" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg/255px-Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg/340px-Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="876" data-file-height="1281" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Am%C3%A9rico_-_D._Pedro_II_na_abertura_da_Assembl%C3%A9ia_Geral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Brazil" title="List of monarchs of Brazil">Emperor of Brazil</a> between 1831 and 1889.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the new Emperor could not exert his constitutional powers until he became of age, a <a href="/wiki/Regency_(government)" class="mw-redirect" title="Regency (government)">regency</a> was set up by the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In the absence of a charismatic figure who could represent a moderate face of power, during this period a series of localized rebellions took place, as the <a href="/wiki/Cabanagem" title="Cabanagem">Cabanagem</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%AA_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Malê Revolt">Malê Revolt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balaiada" title="Balaiada">Balaiada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sabinada" title="Sabinada">Sabinada</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ragamuffin_War" title="Ragamuffin War">Ragamuffin War</a>, which emerged from the dissatisfaction of the provinces with the central power, coupled with old and latent social tensions peculiar of a vast, slaveholding and newly independent <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> This period of internal political and social upheaval, which included the <a href="/wiki/Praieira_revolt" title="Praieira revolt">Praieira revolt</a>, was overcome only at the end of the 1840s, years after the end of the regency, which occurred with the <a href="/wiki/Dom_Pedro_II#Early_coronation" class="mw-redirect" title="Dom Pedro II">premature coronation of Pedro II</a> in 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibidem_Fausto_1999_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibidem_Fausto_1999-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the last phase of the monarchy, internal political debate was centered on the issue of slavery. The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> was abandoned in 1850,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Act" title="Aberdeen Act">Aberdeen Act</a>, but only in <a href="/wiki/Lei_%C3%81urea" title="Lei Áurea">May 1888</a> after a long process of internal mobilization and debate for an ethical and legal dismantling of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Brazil" title="Slavery in Brazil">slavery in the country</a>, was the institution formally abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The foreign affairs in the monarchy were basically related issues with the countries of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a> with which Brazil has borders. Long after the <a href="/wiki/Cisplatine_War" title="Cisplatine War">Cisplatine War</a> that resulted in independence for <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Brazil won three international wars during the 58-year reign of Pedro&#160;II. These were the <a href="/wiki/Platine_War" title="Platine War">Platine War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_War" title="Uruguayan War">Uruguayan War</a> and the devastating <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/War_effort" title="War effort">war effort</a> in Brazilian history.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 November 1889, worn out by years of economic stagnation, in attrition with the majority of Army officers, as well as with rural and financial elites (for different reasons), the monarchy was overthrown by a military coup.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_republic">Early republic</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/First_Brazilian_Republic" title="First Brazilian Republic">First Brazilian Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Brazil)" class="mw-redirect" title="Estado Novo (Brazil)">Estado Novo (Brazil)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Second_Brazilian_Republic" title="Second Brazilian Republic">Second Brazilian Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg/220px-Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg/330px-Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg/440px-Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5799" data-file-height="3574" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_by_Benedito_Calixto_1893.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_Republic_(Brazil)" title="Proclamation of the Republic (Brazil)">Proclamation of the Republic</a></i>, 1893, oil on canvas by <a href="/wiki/Benedito_Calixto" title="Benedito Calixto">Benedito Calixto</a> (1853–1927).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The "early republican government was little more than a military dictatorship, with army dominating affairs both at Rio de Janeiro and in the states. Freedom of the press disappeared and elections were controlled by those in power".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In 1894, following the unfoldings of two severe crises, <a href="/wiki/Encilhamento" title="Encilhamento">an economic</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Revolta_da_Armada" title="Revolta da Armada">a military one</a>, the republican civilians rose to power.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Little by little, <a href="/wiki/Rebellions_and_revolutions_in_Brazil#1st_Republican_period_.281889-1930.29" class="mw-redirect" title="Rebellions and revolutions in Brazil">a cycle of general instability</a> sparked by these crises undermined the regime to such an extent, that in the wake of the murder of his running mate, the defeated opposition presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Get%C3%BAlio_Vargas" title="Getúlio Vargas">Getúlio Vargas</a> supported by most of the military, successfully led the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Revolution_of_1930" title="Brazilian Revolution of 1930">Brazilian Revolution of 1930</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Vargas was supposed to assume power temporarily, but instead closed the Congress, extinguished the Constitution, ruled with emergency powers and replaced the states' governors with his own supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_(cropped).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_%28cropped%29.png/220px-50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_%28cropped%29.png" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_%28cropped%29.png/330px-50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_%28cropped%29.png/440px-50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_%28cropped%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1470" data-file-height="1098" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:50%C2%BA_Anivers%C3%A1rio_da_Rep%C3%BAblica_Brasileira_(cropped).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In half of the first 100 years of republic in Brazil, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">Army</a> exercised power directly or through figures like <a href="/wiki/Get%C3%BAlio_Vargas" title="Getúlio Vargas">Getúlio Vargas</a> (center).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1930s, three major attempts to remove Vargas and his supporters from power occurred. The first was the failed <a href="/wiki/Constitutionalist_Revolution" title="Constitutionalist Revolution">Constitutionalist Revolution</a> of 1932, the second was the anti-fascist <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_uprising_of_1935" title="Brazilian uprising of 1935">Brazilian uprising of 1935</a> led by communists, and the fascist <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Integralism" title="Brazilian Integralism">Integralist Movement</a> attempted a coup in May 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The 1935 uprising created a security crisis in which the Congress transferred more power to the executive. The 1937 <i>coup d'état</i> resulted in the cancellation of the 1938 election, installed Vargas as a dictator, and began the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Brazil)" class="mw-redirect" title="Estado Novo (Brazil)">Estado Novo</a> era, noted for government brutality and censorship of the press.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>In foreign policy, the success in resolving border disputes with neighboring countries in the early years of the republican period,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> was followed by a failed attempt to exert a prominent role in the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> after <a href="/wiki/Brazil_during_World_War_I" title="Brazil during World War I">its involvement</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> Brazil remained neutral until August 1942, when <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Expeditionary_Force" title="Brazilian Expeditionary Force">the country entered</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">allied side</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> after suffering <a href="/wiki/Submarine_warfare#Atlantic_ocean" title="Submarine warfare">retaliations</a> undertaken by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861%E2%80%931946)#Fascism_.281922.E2.80.931943.29" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861–1946)">Fascist Italy</a>, due to the country having severed diplomatic relations with <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/1942_Rio_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="1942 Rio Conference">Pan-American Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the allied victory in 1945 and the end of the Nazi-fascist regimes in Europe, Vargas's position became unsustainable and he was swiftly overthrown in another military coup, with Democracy being "reinstated" by the same army that had discontinued it 15 years before.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Vargas committed suicide in August 1954 amid a political crisis, after having returned to power by election in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_era">Contemporary era</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_military_government" title="Brazilian military government">Brazilian military government</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil_since_1985" title="History of Brazil since 1985">History of Brazil since 1985</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg/220px-0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg/330px-0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg/440px-0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1276" data-file-height="855" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:0741_NOV_B_05_Esplanada_dos_Ministerios_Brasilia_DF_03_09_1959.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Construction of <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, the new capital, in 1959</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several brief interim governments succeeded after Vargas's suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Juscelino_Kubitschek" title="Juscelino Kubitschek">Juscelino Kubitschek</a> became president in 1956 and assumed a conciliatory posture towards the <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(politics)" title="Opposition (politics)">political opposition</a> that allowed him to govern without major crises.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The economy and industrial sector grew remarkably,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> but his greatest achievement was the construction of the new capital city of <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, inaugurated in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> His successor was <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A2nio_Quadros" title="Jânio Quadros">Jânio Quadros</a>, who resigned in 1961 less than a year after taking office.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> His vice-president, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Goulart" title="João Goulart">João Goulart</a>, assumed the presidency, but aroused strong political opposition<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and was <a href="/wiki/1964_Brazilian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1964 Brazilian coup d'état">deposed in April 1964 by a coup</a> that resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_military_government" title="Brazilian military government">military regime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new regime was intended to be transitory<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> but it gradually closed in on itself and became a full dictatorship with the promulgation of the Fifth Institutional Act in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-Gaspari_p.35_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaspari_p.35-120">[120]</a></sup> The oppression was not limited to only those who resorted to guerrilla tactics to fight the regime, but also reached institutional opponents, artists, journalists and other members of civil society,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> inside and outside the country (through the infamous "<a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Despite its brutality, like other <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">totalitarian regimes</a> in history, due to an economic boom, known as an "economic miracle", the regime reached its highest level of popularity in the early 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg/220px-Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg/330px-Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg/440px-Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2595" data-file-height="1772" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulyssesguimaraesconstituicao.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ulysses_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Ulysses Guimarães">Ulysses Guimarães</a> holding the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Constitution of 1988</a> in his hands.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Slowly however, the wear and tear of years of dictatorial power that had not slowed the repression, even after the defeat of the leftist guerrillas,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> plus the inability to deal with the economic crises of the period and popular pressure, made an opening policy inevitable, which from the regime side was led by Generals <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Geisel" title="Ernesto Geisel">Geisel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golbery_do_Couto_e_Silva" title="Golbery do Couto e Silva">Golbery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> With the enactment of the Amnesty Law in 1979, Brazil began its slow return to democracy, which would be completed during the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibidem_Fausto_1999_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibidem_Fausto_1999-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Civilians returned to power in 1985 when José Sarney assumed the presidency, becoming unpopular during his tenure due to his failure in controlling the economic crisis and hyperinflation inherited from the military regime.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Sarney's unsuccessful government allowed the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_presidential_election,_1989" title="Brazilian presidential election, 1989">election in 1989</a> of the almost unknown <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Collor_de_Mello" title="Fernando Collor de Mello">Fernando Collor</a>, who was subsequently impeached by the National Congress in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Collor was succeeded by his Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Itamar_Franco" title="Itamar Franco">Itamar Franco</a>, who appointed <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Henrique_Cardoso" title="Fernando Henrique Cardoso">Fernando Henrique Cardoso</a> as Minister of Finance. In 1994, Cardoso produced a highly successful <a href="/wiki/Plano_Real" title="Plano Real">Plano Real</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> that, after decades of failed economic plans made by previous governments attempting to curb hyperinflation, finally granted stability to the Brazilian economy,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> leading Cardoso to be <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_presidential_election,_1994" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian presidential election, 1994">elected that year</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_presidential_election,_1998" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian presidential election, 1998">again in 1998</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>The peaceful transition of power from Fernando Henrique to his main opposition leader, <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brazilian_presidential_election,_2002" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian presidential election, 2002">elected in 2002</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_presidential_election,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian presidential election, 2006">re-elected in 2006</a>), was seen as a proof that Brazil had finally succeeded in achieving a long-sought political stability.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> However, sparked by indignation and frustrations accumulated over decades (against corruption, <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a>, inefficiencies of political <a href="/wiki/The_Establishment" title="The Establishment">establishment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_service" title="Public service">public service</a>), <a href="/wiki/2013_protests_in_Brazil" title="2013 protests in Brazil">numerous peaceful protests erupted in Brazil</a> from the middle of first term of <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> (who succeeded Lula <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_presidential_election,_2010" title="Brazilian presidential election, 2010">in 2010</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Enhanced by a political and economic crises with evidences of involvement of politicians from all main political parties in several <a href="/wiki/Bribery" title="Bribery">bribery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tax_evasion" title="Tax evasion">tax evasion</a> schemes,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_protests_in_Brazil" title="2015–16 protests in Brazil">large street protests for and against her</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Rousseff <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">was impeached</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Congress">Brazilian Congress</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Brazil" title="Geography of Brazil">Geography of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brazil_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Brazil_topo.jpg/330px-Brazil_topo.jpg" width="330" height="334" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Brazil_topo.jpg/495px-Brazil_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Brazil_topo.jpg/660px-Brazil_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1419" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brazil_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Topographic map of Brazil.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil occupies a large area along the eastern coast of South America and includes much of the continent's interior,<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_6_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_6-142">[142]</a></sup> sharing land borders with <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> to the south; <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> to the southwest; <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> to the west; <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> to the northwest; and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (French overseas region of <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>) to the north. It shares a border with every South American country except <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>. It also encompasses a number of oceanic <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagos</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Fernando_de_Noronha" title="Fernando de Noronha">Fernando de Noronha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocas_Atoll" title="Rocas Atoll">Rocas Atoll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_and_Saint_Paul_Archipelago" title="Saint Peter and Saint Paul Archipelago">Saint Peter and Paul Rocks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trindade_and_Martim_Vaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Trindade and Martim Vaz">Trindade and Martim Vaz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Geo_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Geo-15">[15]</a></sup> Its size, relief, climate, and natural resources make Brazil geographically diverse.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_6_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_6-142">[142]</a></sup> Including its <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> islands, Brazil lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_parallel_north" title="6th parallel north">6°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/34th_parallel_south" title="34th parallel south">34°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/28th_meridian_west" title="28th meridian west">28°</a> and <a href="/wiki/74th_meridian_west" title="74th meridian west">74°W</a>.</p>
<p>Brazil is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">fifth largest</a> country in the world, and third largest in the Americas, with a total area of 8,515,767.049&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (3,287,956&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Area_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Area-143">[143]</a></sup> including 55,455&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (21,411&#160;sq&#160;mi) of water.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Geo_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Geo-15">[15]</a></sup> It spans four <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">time zones</a>; from <a href="/wiki/UTC-05" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC-05">UTC−5</a> comprising the state of <a href="/wiki/Acre_(state)" title="Acre (state)">Acre</a> and the westernmost portion of <a href="/wiki/Amazonas_(Brazilian_state)" title="Amazonas (Brazilian state)">Amazonas</a>, to <a href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%9204" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC−04">UTC−4</a> in the western states, to <a href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%9203" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC−03">UTC−3</a> in the eastern states (the <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Brazil" title="Time in Brazil">national time</a>) and <a href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%9202" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC−02">UTC−2</a> in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Brazil" title="List of islands of Brazil">Atlantic islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timezones_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timezones-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil is the only country in the world that has the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a> running through it. It is also the only country to have contiguous territory both inside and outside the tropics. Brazilian topography is also diverse and includes hills, mountains, plains, highlands, and scrublands. Much of the terrain lies between 200 metres (660&#160;ft) and 800 metres (2,600&#160;ft) in elevation.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_7_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_7-145">[145]</a></sup> The main upland area occupies most of the southern half of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_7_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_7-145">[145]</a></sup> The northwestern parts of the plateau consist of broad, rolling terrain broken by low, rounded hills.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_7_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_7-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>The southeastern section is more rugged, with a complex mass of ridges and mountain ranges reaching elevations of up to 1,200 metres (3,900&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_7_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_7-145">[145]</a></sup> These ranges include the <a href="/wiki/Mantiqueira_Mountains" title="Mantiqueira Mountains">Mantiqueira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Espinha%C3%A7o_Mountains" title="Espinhaço Mountains">Espinhaço</a> mountains and the <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar" title="Serra do Mar">Serra do Mar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_7_145-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_7-145">[145]</a></sup> In the north, the <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Shield" title="Guiana Shield">Guiana Highlands</a> form a major drainage divide, separating rivers that flow south into the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon Basin</a> from rivers that empty into the <a href="/wiki/Orinoco" title="Orinoco">Orinoco River</a> system, in Venezuela, to the north. The highest point in Brazil is the <a href="/wiki/Pico_da_Neblina" title="Pico da Neblina">Pico da Neblina</a> at 2,994 metres (9,823&#160;ft), and the lowest is the Atlantic Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Geo_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Geo-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil has a dense and complex system of rivers, one of the world's most extensive, with eight major drainage basins, all of which drain into the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_8_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_8-146">[146]</a></sup> Major rivers include the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a> (the world's second-longest river and the largest in terms of volume of water), the <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">Paraná</a> and its major tributary the <a href="/wiki/Iguazu_River" title="Iguazu River">Iguaçu</a> (which includes the <a href="/wiki/Iguazu_Falls" title="Iguazu Falls">Iguazu Falls</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Negro_(Amazon)" title="Rio Negro (Amazon)">Negro</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Francisco_River" title="São Francisco River">São Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xingu_River" title="Xingu River">Xingu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira_River" title="Madeira River">Madeira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tapaj%C3%B3s" title="Tapajós">Tapajós</a> rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_8_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_8-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

</div>

</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Brazil" title="Climate of Brazil">Climate of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_of_Brazil.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Climate_of_Brazil.tif/lossless-page1-220px-Climate_of_Brazil.tif.png" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Climate_of_Brazil.tif/lossless-page1-330px-Climate_of_Brazil.tif.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Climate_of_Brazil.tif/lossless-page1-440px-Climate_of_Brazil.tif.png 2x" data-file-width="2624" data-file-height="2508" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_of_Brazil.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brazil map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate of Brazil comprises a wide range of weather conditions across a large area and varied topography, but most of the country is tropical.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Geo_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Geo-15">[15]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen system</a>, Brazil hosts five major climatic subtypes: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">equatorial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semiarid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">highland tropical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperateness">temperate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical</a>. The different climatic conditions produce environments ranging from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">equatorial rainforests</a> in the north and semiarid deserts in the northeast, to <a href="/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest" title="Temperate coniferous forest">temperate coniferous forests</a> in the south and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_grasslands,_savannas,_and_shrublands" title="Tropical and subtropical grasslands, savannas, and shrublands">tropical savannas</a> in central Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-147">[147]</a></sup> Many regions have starkly different <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BT_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>An equatorial climate characterizes much of northern Brazil. There is no real <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>, but there are some variations in the period of the year when most rain falls.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-147">[147]</a></sup> Temperatures average 25&#160;°C (77&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-BT_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-149">[149]</a></sup> with more significant temperature variation between night and day than between seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over central Brazil rainfall is more seasonal, characteristic of a savanna climate.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-148">[148]</a></sup> This region is as extensive as the Amazon basin but has a very different climate as it lies farther south at a higher altitude.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-147">[147]</a></sup> In the interior northeast, seasonal rainfall is even more extreme. The semiarid climatic region generally receives less than 800 millimetres (31.5&#160;in) of rain,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> most of which generally falls in a period of three to five months of the year<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> and occasionally less than this, creating long periods of drought.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_148-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-148">[148]</a></sup> Brazil's 1877–78 <i><a href="/wiki/Grande_Seca" title="Grande Seca">Grande Seca</a></i> (Great Drought), the worst in Brazil's history,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> caused approximately half a million deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> A similarly devastating drought occurred in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>South of Bahia, near the coasts, and more southerly most of the state of São Paulo, the distribution of rainfall changes, with rain falling throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_147-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-147">[147]</a></sup> The south enjoys subtropical conditions, with cool winters and average annual temperatures not exceeding 18&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F);<sup id="cite_ref-BT_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-149">[149]</a></sup> winter frosts and <a href="/wiki/Snow_in_Brazil" title="Snow in Brazil">snowfall</a> are not rare in the highest areas.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Weather_147-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Weather-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_9_148-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_9-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class='gallerycaption'>Climate of Brazil</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">
<div style="width: 182px">
