<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_environment">Biodiversity and environment</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">Wildlife of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Brazil" title="Deforestation in Brazil">Deforestation in Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Conservation_in_Brazil" title="Conservation in Brazil">Conservation in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazil's large territory comprises different ecosystems, such as the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>, recognized as having the greatest <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biological diversity</a> in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-WWF_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-155">[155]</a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Forest" title="Atlantic Forest">Atlantic Forest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cerrado" title="Cerrado">Cerrado</a>, sustaining the greatest biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-156">[156]</a></sup> In the south, the <a href="/wiki/Araucaria" title="Araucaria">Araucaria</a> pine forest grows under temperate conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-156">[156]</a></sup> The rich wildlife of Brazil reflects the variety of natural habitats. Scientists estimate that the total number of <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">plant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">animal species</a> in Brazil could approach four million, mostly invertebrates.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_156-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_CIAT_(5).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg/220px-Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg/330px-Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg/440px-Amazon_CIAT_%285%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_CIAT_(5).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>, the richest and most biodiverse rainforest in the world.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Larger mammals include carnivores <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">pumas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">jaguars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocelot" title="Ocelot">ocelots</a>, rare <a href="/wiki/Bush_dog" title="Bush dog">bush dogs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">foxes</a>, and herbivores <a href="/wiki/Peccary" title="Peccary">peccaries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapir" title="Tapir">tapirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">anteaters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sloth" title="Sloth">sloths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">opossums</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armadillo" title="Armadillo">armadillos</a>. <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">Deer</a> are plentiful in the south, and many species of <a href="/wiki/New_World_monkey" title="New World monkey">New World monkeys</a> are found in the northern <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rain forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_10_156-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_10-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Concern for the environment has grown in response to global interest in environmental issues.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_11_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_11-158">[158]</a></sup> Brazil's Amazon Basin is home to an extremely diverse array of fish species, including the <a href="/wiki/Red-bellied_piranha" title="Red-bellied piranha">red-bellied piranha</a>. Despite its reputation as a ferocious freshwater fish, the red-bellied piranha is actually a generally timid scavenger. Biodiversity can contribute to <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, livestock, forestry and fisheries extraction. However, almost all economically exploited species of plants, such as soybeans and coffee, or animals, such as chickens, are imported from other countries, and the economic use of native species still crawls. In the Brazilian GDP, the forest sector represents just over 1% and fishing 0.4%.</p>
<p>The natural heritage of Brazil is severely threatened by cattle ranching and agriculture, logging, mining, resettlement, oil and gas extraction, over-fishing, wildlife trade, dams and infrastructure, water pollution, climate change, fire, and invasive species.<sup id="cite_ref-WWF_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-155">[155]</a></sup> In many areas of the country, the natural environment is threatened by development.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Construction of highways has opened up previously remote areas for agriculture and settlement; dams have flooded valleys and inundated wildlife habitats; and mines have scarred and polluted the landscape.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_11_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_11-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> At least 70 dams are said to be planned for the Amazon region, including the controversial <a href="/wiki/Belo_Monte_Dam" title="Belo Monte Dam">Belo Monte</a> hydroelectric dam.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class='gallerycaption'>Biodiversity of Brazil</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 152px">
<div style="width: 152px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">

</div>

<p><a href="/wiki/Toco_toucan" title="Toco toucan">Toco toucan</a>, a Brazilian symbol, a country with one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Brazil" title="List of birds of Brazil">largest variety of birds</a> in the world.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">

</div>

</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Brazil" title="Politics of Brazil">Politics of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Brazil" title="Federal government of Brazil">Federal government of Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Brazil" title="Elections in Brazil">Elections in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Planalto_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Planalto_panorama.jpg/220px-Planalto_panorama.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Planalto_panorama.jpg/330px-Planalto_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Planalto_panorama.jpg/440px-Planalto_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="2840" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Planalto_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_do_Planalto" title="Palácio do Planalto">Palácio do Planalto</a> ("Plateau Palace"), the official workplace of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The form of government is that of a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federative</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The president is both head of state and head of government of the Union and is elected for a four-year term,<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> with the possibility of re-election for a second successive term. The current president is <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">Michel Temer</a>, who replaced <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> after her <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">impeachment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-162">[162]</a></sup> The President appoints the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State" title="Minister of State">Ministers of State</a>, who assist in government.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> Legislative houses in each political entity are the main source of law in Brazil. The <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress</a> is the Federation's bicameral legislature, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Brazil">Chamber of Deputies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Brazil">Federal Senate</a>. Judiciary authorities exercise jurisdictional duties almost exclusively. Brazil is a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Brazilian Federation is the "indissoluble union" of the States, the Municipalities and the Federal District.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The Union, the states and the Federal District, and the municipalities, are the "spheres of government". The <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a> is set on five fundamental principles:<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> sovereignty, citizenship, dignity of human beings, the social values of labour and freedom of enterprise, and political pluralism. The classic tripartite branches of government (executive, legislative and judicial under a checks and balances system) are formally established by the Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The executive and legislative are organized <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">independently in all three spheres of government</a>, while the judiciary is organized only at the federal and state/Federal District spheres.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg/220px-Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg/330px-Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg/440px-Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1162" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brasilia_Congresso_Nacional_05_2007_221.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress of Brazil</a>, seat of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All members of the executive and legislative branches are directly elected.<sup id="cite_ref-embassy_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embassy-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Judges and other judicial officials are appointed after passing entry exams.<sup id="cite_ref-embassy_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embassy-164">[164]</a></sup> For most of its democratic history, Brazil has had a multi-party system, proportional representation. Voting is compulsory for the literate between 18 and 70 years old and optional for illiterates and those between 16 and 18 or beyond 70.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Together with several smaller parties, four political parties stand out: <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_(Brazil)" title="Workers' Party (Brazil)">Workers' Party</a> (PT), <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Social_Democracy_Party" title="Brazilian Social Democracy Party">Brazilian Social Democracy Party</a> (PSDB), <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Democratic_Movement_Party" title="Brazilian Democratic Movement Party">Brazilian Democratic Movement Party</a> (PMDB) and <a href="/wiki/Democrats_(Brazil)" title="Democrats (Brazil)">Democrats</a> (DEM). Fifteen political parties are represented in Congress. It is common for politicians to switch parties, and thus the proportion of congressional seats held by particular parties changes regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Almost all governmental and administrative functions are exercised by authorities and agencies affiliated to the Executive.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Brazil" title="Law of Brazil">Law of Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Brazil" title="Law enforcement in Brazil">Law enforcement in Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Brazil" title="Crime in Brazil">Crime in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazilian law is based on <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman</a>-<a href="/wiki/Germania" title="Germania">Germanic</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> traditions<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> concepts prevail over common law practice. Most of Brazilian law is codified, although non-codified statutes also represent a substantial part, playing a complementary role. Court decisions set out interpretive guidelines; however, they are seldom binding on other specific cases. Doctrinal works and the works of academic jurists have strong influence in law creation and in law cases.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Supremo_Brasil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Supremo_Brasil.jpg/220px-Supremo_Brasil.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Supremo_Brasil.jpg/330px-Supremo_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Supremo_Brasil.jpg/440px-Supremo_Brasil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Supremo_Brasil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Federal Court of Brazil">Supreme Federal Court of Brazil</a> serves primarily as the Constitutional Court of the country.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The legal system is based on the Federal Constitution, which was promulgated on 5 October 1988, and is the fundamental law of Brazil. All other legislation and court decisions must conform to its rules.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> As of April 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brazil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there have been 53 amendments. States have their own constitutions, which must not contradict the Federal Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Municipalities and the Federal District have "organic laws" (<span lang="pt"><i>leis orgânicas</i></span>), which act in a similar way to constitutions.<sup id="cite_ref-DeffentiBarral2011_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeffentiBarral2011-171">[171]</a></sup> Legislative entities are the main source of statutes, although in certain matters judiciary and executive bodies may enact legal norms.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> Jurisdiction is administered by the judiciary entities, although in rare situations the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Federal Constitution</a> allows the Federal Senate to pass on legal judgments.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> There are also specialized military, labor, and electoral courts.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The highest court is the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Federal_Court" title="Supreme Federal Court">Supreme Federal Court</a>.</p>
<p>This system has been criticized over the last few decades for the slow pace of decision-making. Lawsuits on appeal may take several years to resolve, and in some cases more than a decade elapses before definitive rulings.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the Supreme Federal Tribunal was the first court in the world to transmit its sessions on television, and also via <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> More recently, in December 2009, the Supreme Court adopted <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> to display items on the day planner of the ministers, to inform the daily actions of the Court and the most important decisions made by them.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Armed_Forces" title="Brazilian Armed Forces">Brazilian Armed Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg/220px-US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg/330px-US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg/440px-US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3965" data-file-height="2832" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_100316-N-9116F-001_A_Brazilian_U.N._peacekeeper_walks_with_Haitian_children_during_a_patrol_in_Cite_Soleil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">Brazilian Army</a> participating in a <a href="/wiki/UN_peacekeeping" class="mw-redirect" title="UN peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping</a> mission in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The armed forces of Brazil are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">second largest</a> in Latin America by active personnel and the largest in terms of military equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> It consists of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">Brazilian Army</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army_Aviation_Command" title="Brazilian Army Aviation Command">Army Aviation Command</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Navy" title="Brazilian Navy">Brazilian Navy</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Marine_Corps" title="Brazilian Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Naval_Aviation" title="Brazilian Naval Aviation">Naval Aviation</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Air_Force" title="Brazilian Air Force">Brazilian Air Force</a>. Brazil's <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> policy gives it one of the world's largest military forces, estimated at more than 1.6 million <a href="/wiki/Military_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Military Reserve">reservist</a> annually.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Numbering close to 236,000 active personnel,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> the Brazilian Army has the largest number of armored vehicles in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, including armored transports and <a href="/wiki/Battle_tank" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle tank">tanks</a><sup id="cite_ref-militarypower1_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-militarypower1-179">[179]</a></sup> It is also unique in Latin America for its large, elite forces specializing in unconventional missions, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Special_Operations_Command" title="Brazilian Special Operations Command">Brazilian Special Operations Command</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> and the versatile Strategic Rapid Action Force, made up of highly mobilized and prepared (Special Operations Brigade, <a href="/wiki/Parachute_Infantry_Brigade_(Brazil)" title="Parachute Infantry Brigade (Brazil)">Infantry Brigade Parachutist</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> 1st Jungle Infantry Battalion (Airmobile)<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> and 12th Brigade Light Infantry (Airmobile)<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> able to act anywhere in the country, on short notice, to counter external aggression.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The states' <a href="/wiki/Military_Police_(Brazil)" title="Military Police (Brazil)">Military Police</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Military_Firefighters_Corps" title="Military Firefighters Corps">Military Firefighters Corps</a> are described as an ancillary forces of the Army by the constitution, but are under the control of each state's governor.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg/330px-Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg" width="330" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg/495px-Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg/660px-Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="1473" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Various_aircraft_participate_in_the_Cruzeiro_Do_Sul_2010_exercises.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Various aircraft participate in the <a href="/wiki/South_America_air_forces_maneuvers" title="South America air forces maneuvers">CRUZEX</a> exercise on 11 November 2010, at <a href="/wiki/Natal_Air_Force_Base" title="Natal Air Force Base">Natal Air Force Base</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Navy once operated some of the most powerful warships in the world with the two <a href="/wiki/Minas_Geraes-class_battleship" title="Minas Geraes-class battleship"><i>Minas Geraes</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnoughts</a>, which sparked a <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">South American dreadnought race</a> between Argentina, Brazil, and Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Today, it is a <a href="/wiki/Green-water_navy" title="Green-water navy">green water</a> force and has a group of specialized elite in retaking ships and naval facilities, <a href="/wiki/GRUMEC" title="GRUMEC">GRUMEC</a>, unit specially trained to protect Brazilian oil platforms along its coast.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> It's the only navy in Latin America that operates an <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_aircraft_carrier_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(A12)" title="Brazilian aircraft carrier São Paulo (A12)">NAe São Paulo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> and one of the ten navies of the world to operate this type of ship.<sup id="cite_ref-militarypower1_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-militarypower1-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Air Force, it is the largest in Latin America has about 700 manned aircraft in service and effective about 67,000 personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil has not been invaded since 1865 during the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Additionally, Brazil has no contested territorial disputes with any of its neighbours<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> and neither does it have rivalries, like Chile and Bolivia have with each other.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> The Brazilian military has also three times intervened militarily to overthrow the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Brazil">Brazilian government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-revistaepoca.globo.com_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revistaepoca.globo.com-196">[196]</a></sup> It has built a tradition of participating in UN <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> missions such as in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<center>
<table class="toccolours" style="float:center; margin:0 0 1em 1em; border:1px #ddd solid;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Brazil" title="Foreign relations of Brazil">Foreign relations of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Itamaraty.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Itamaraty.jpg/220px-Itamaraty.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Itamaraty.jpg/330px-Itamaraty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Itamaraty.jpg/440px-Itamaraty.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Itamaraty.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Itamaraty_Palace" title="Itamaraty Palace">Itamaraty Palace</a>, the seat of <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Brazil)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Brazil)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil's international relations are based on Article 4 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Federal Constitution</a>, which establishes <a href="/wiki/Non-interventionism" title="Non-interventionism">non-intervention</a>, <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internationalism_(politics)" title="Internationalism (politics)">international cooperation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Peacebuilding" title="Peacebuilding">peaceful settlement of conflicts</a> as the guiding principles of Brazil's relationship with other countries and multilateral organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the Constitution, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President</a> has ultimate authority over foreign policy, while the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">Congress</a> is tasked with reviewing and considering all diplomatic nominations and <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">international treaties</a>, as well as legislation relating to Brazilian foreign policy.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil's foreign policy is a by-product of the country's unique position as a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, a leader among <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>, and an emerging <a href="/wiki/World_power" class="mw-redirect" title="World power">world power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> Brazilian foreign policy has generally been based on the principles of <a href="/wiki/Multilateralism" title="Multilateralism">multilateralism</a>, peaceful dispute settlement, and non-intervention in the affairs of other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>An increasingly well-developed tool of Brazil's foreign policy is providing aid as a donor to other developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-202">[202]</a></sup> Brazil does not just use its growing economic strength to provide financial aid, but it also provides high levels of expertise and most importantly of all, a quiet non-confrontational diplomacy to improve governance levels.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-202">[202]</a></sup> Total aid is estimated to be around $1 billion per year that includes:<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_202-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png/330px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png" width="330" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png/495px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png/660px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Brazil.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Brazil" title="List of diplomatic missions in Brazil">Diplomatic missions of Brazil</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>technical cooperation of around $480 million ($30 million in 2010 provided directly by the Brazilian Cooperation Agency (ABC))</li>
<li>an estimated $450 million for in-kind expertise provided by Brazilian institutions specialising in technical cooperation</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, Brazil manages a peacekeeping mission in <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">Haiti</a> ($350 million) and makes in-kind contributions to the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> ($300 million).<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_202-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-202">[202]</a></sup> This is in addition to humanitarian assistance and contributions to multilateral development agencies. The scale of this aid places it on par with China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_202-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-202">[202]</a></sup> The Brazilian South-South aid has been described as a "global model in waiting."<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_crime">Law enforcement and crime</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Brazil" title="Law enforcement in Brazil">Law enforcement in Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Brazil" title="Crime in Brazil">Crime in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg/220px-Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg/330px-Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg/440px-Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3603" data-file-height="2309" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Helic%C3%B3ptero_PF.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Helicopter of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Police Department">Federal Police Department</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Brazil, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Constitution</a> establishes five different police agencies for law enforcement: <a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Police Department">Federal Police Department</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Highway_Police" title="Federal Highway Police">Federal Highway Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Railroad_Police" title="Federal Railroad Police">Federal Railroad Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_Police_(Brazil)" title="Military Police (Brazil)">Military Police</a> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_Police_(Brazil)" title="Civil Police (Brazil)">Civil Police</a>. Of these, the first three are affiliated with federal authorities and the last two are subordinate to state governments. All police forces are the responsibility of the executive branch of any of the federal or state powers.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Security_Force" title="National Public Security Force">National Public Security Force</a> also can act in public disorder situations arising anywhere in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>The country still has above-average levels of violent crime and particularly high levels of gun violence and homicide. In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) estimated the number of 32 deaths per 100,000 inhabitants, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">highest rates of intentional homicide of the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The number considered tolerable by the WHO is about 10 homicides per 100,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> However, there are differences between the crime rates in the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">Brazilian states</a>. While in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a> the homicide rate registered in 2013 was 10.8 deaths per 100,000 inhabitants, in <a href="/wiki/Alagoas" title="Alagoas">Alagoas</a> it was 64.7 homicides per 100,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil also has high levels of incarceration and the third largest prison population in the world (behind only <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>), with an estimated total of approximately 700,000 prisoners around the country (June 2014), an increase of about 300% compared to the index registered in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> The high number of prisoners eventually overloaded the Brazilian prison system, leading to a shortfall of about two hundred thousand accommodations.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>

<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">States of Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Brazil" title="Municipalities of Brazil">Municipalities of Brazil</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Brazil" title="Regions of Brazil">Regions of Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazil is a federation composed of 26 <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">States</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Federal_District_(Brazil)" title="Federal District (Brazil)">Federal district</a> (which contains the capital city, <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">Municipalities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> States have autonomous administrations, collect their own taxes and receive a share of taxes collected by the Federal government. They have a governor and a unicameral legislative body elected directly by their voters. They also have independent Courts of Law for common justice. Despite this, states have much less autonomy to create their own laws than in the United States. For example, criminal and civil laws can be voted by only the federal bicameral Congress and are uniform throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The states and the federal district may be grouped into regions: <a href="/wiki/Northern_Region,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Region, Brazil">Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Northeast Region, Brazil">Northeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central-West_Region,_Brazil" title="Central-West Region, Brazil">Central-West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Southeast Region, Brazil">Southeast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Region,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Region, Brazil">Southern</a>. The Brazilian regions are merely geographical, not political or administrative divisions, and they do not have any specific form of government. Although defined by law, Brazilian regions are useful mainly for statistical purposes, and also to define the distribution of federal funds in development projects.</p>
<p>Municipalities, as the states, have autonomous administrations, collect their own taxes and receive a share of taxes collected by the Union and state government.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o_17-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitui.C3.A7.C3.A3o-17">[17]</a></sup> Each has a mayor and an elected legislative body, but no separate Court of Law. Indeed, a Court of Law organized by the state can encompass many municipalities in a single justice administrative division called <i><a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarca</a></i> (county).</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Economy of Brazil</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">Brazilian real</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:443px;max-width:443px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:237px;max-width:237px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/235px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg" width="235" height="125" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/353px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/470px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3612" data-file-height="1918" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Quotes panel of <a href="/wiki/BM%26F_Bovespa" title="BM&amp;F Bovespa">BM&amp;F Bovespa</a>, in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, the country's <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_(15414135738).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/200px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg" width="200" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/300px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg/400px-Apresenta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_KC-390_%2815414135738%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1136" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
<center>A <a href="/wiki/Embraer_KC-390" title="Embraer KC-390">KC-390</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_transport_aircraft" title="Military transport aircraft">military transport aircraft</a>, developed by Brazilian company <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a>, the third largest producer of civil aircraft, after <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></center>
</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil is the largest national economy in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">world's eight largest economy</a> at market exchange rates and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">seventh largest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP), according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>. Brazil has a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> with abundant natural resources. After rapid growth in preceding decades, the country <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%932016_Brazilian_economic_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="2014–2016 Brazilian economic recession">entered an ongoing recession in 2014</a> amid a political corruption scandal and nationwide protests.</p>
<p>Its GDP (PPP) per capita was $15,048 in 2016<sup id="cite_ref-imf_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf-8">[8]</a></sup> putting Brazil in the 77th position according to IMF data. Active in <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service sectors</a> Brazil has a labor force of over a 107 million (ranking 6th worldwide) and unemployment of 6.2% (ranking 64th worldwide).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Econ_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Econ-211">[211]</a></sup> The country has been expanding its presence in international financial and <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">commodities markets</a>, and is one of a group of four emerging economies called the <a href="/wiki/BRIC" title="BRIC">BRIC countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Brazil has been the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Brazil" title="Coffee production in Brazil">producer of coffee</a> for the last 150 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Neilson102_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neilson102-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arroz_097.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Arroz_097.jpg/220px-Arroz_097.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Arroz_097.jpg/330px-Arroz_097.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Arroz_097.jpg/440px-Arroz_097.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arroz_097.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Combine_harvester" title="Combine harvester">Combine harvester</a> in a rice plantation in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a>. Brazil is the third largest exporter of agricultural products in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-exporta.C3.A7.C3.A3oagr.C3.ADcola_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exporta.C3.A7.C3.A3oagr.C3.ADcola-213">[213]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg/220px-Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg" width="220" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg/330px-Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg/440px-Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1783" data-file-height="2458" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Bank_of_Brazil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Brazil" title="Central Bank of Brazil">Central Bank of Brazil</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil has become the fourth largest car market in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Major export products include <a href="/wiki/Fixed-wing_aircraft" title="Fixed-wing aircraft">aircraft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_equipment" title="Electrical equipment">electrical equipment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Footwear" title="Footwear">footwear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_juice" title="Orange juice">orange juice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybeans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corned_beef" title="Corned beef">corned beef</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> In total, Brazil ranks 23rd worldwide in <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">value of exports</a>.</p>
<p>Brazil pegged its currency, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">real</a>, to the U.S. dollar in 1994. However, after the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">East Asian financial crisis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis" title="1998 Russian financial crisis">Russian default</a> in 1998<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> and the series of adverse financial events that followed it, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Brazil" title="Central Bank of Brazil">Central Bank of Brazil</a> temporarily changed its <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> to a managed-float<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> scheme while undergoing a <a href="/wiki/Currency_crisis" title="Currency crisis">currency crisis</a>, until definitively changing the exchange regime to <a href="/wiki/Free-float" class="mw-redirect" title="Free-float">free-float</a> in January 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil received an International Monetary Fund rescue package in mid-2002 of $30.4&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> then a record sum. Brazil's central bank paid back the IMF loan in 2005, although it was not due to be repaid until 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> One of the issues the Central Bank of Brazil recently dealt with was an excess of speculative short-term capital inflows to the country, which may have contributed to a fall in the value of the U.S. dollar against the real during that period.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Nonetheless, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> (FDI), related to long-term, less speculative investment in production, is estimated to be $193.8&#160;billion for 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Inflation monitoring and control currently plays a major part in the Central bank's role of setting out short-term <a href="/wiki/Interest_rate" title="Interest rate">interest rates</a> as a monetary policy measure.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 1993 and 2010, 7012 <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">mergers &amp; acquisitions</a> with a total known value of $707 billion with the involvement of Brazilian firms have been announced.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> The year 2010 was a new record in terms of value with 115 billion USD of transactions. The largest transaction with involvement of Brazilian companies has been: <a href="/wiki/Vale_(mining_company)" title="Vale (mining company)">Cia. Vale do Rio Doce</a> acquired <a href="/wiki/Vale_Inco" class="mw-redirect" title="Vale Inco">Inco</a> in a tender offer valued at US$18.9 billion.</p>
<p>Corruption costs Brazil almost $41 billion a year alone, with 69.9% of the country's firms identifying the issue as a major constraint in successfully penetrating the global market.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Local government corruption is so prevalent that voters perceive it as a problem only if it surpasses certain levels, and only if a local media e.g. a radio station is present to divulge the findings of corruption charges.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> Initiatives, like this exposure, strengthen awareness which is indicated by the Transparency International's <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>; ranking Brazil 69th out of 178 countries in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power" title="Purchasing power">purchasing power</a> in Brazil is eroded by the so-called <a href="/wiki/Brazil_cost" title="Brazil cost">Brazil cost</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-brcost_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brcost-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Components_and_energy">Components and energy</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Brazil" title="Agriculture in Brazil">Agriculture in Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Brazil" title="Mining in Brazil">Mining in Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industry_in_Brazil" title="Industry in Brazil">Industry in Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_Brazil" title="Energy policy of Brazil">Energy policy of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_platform_P-51_(Brazil)-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg/220px-Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg/330px-Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg/440px-Oil_platform_P-51_%28Brazil%29-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2657" data-file-height="1772" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_platform_P-51_(Brazil)-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
P-51, an <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">oil platform</a> of <a href="/wiki/Petrobras" title="Petrobras">Petrobras</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazil's diversified economy includes agriculture, industry, and a wide range of services.<sup id="cite_ref-BansalPhatak2009_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BansalPhatak2009-229">[229]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Brazil" title="Agriculture in Brazil">Agriculture</a> and allied sectors like <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> accounted for 5.1% of the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_GDP_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_GDP-230">[230]</a></sup> Brazil is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_producing_countries_of_agricultural_commodities" title="List of largest producing countries of agricultural commodities">largest producer</a> of oranges, coffee, sugar cane, cassava and sisal, soybeans and papayas.<sup id="cite_ref-Luck1998_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luck1998-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Industry_in_Brazil" title="Industry in Brazil">industry</a>&#160;– from <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemicals</a> to <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Durable_good" title="Durable good">consumer durables</a> – accounted for 30.8% of the gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_GDP_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_GDP-230">[230]</a></sup> Industry is highly concentrated in metropolitan São Paulo, Rio de Janeiro, <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GiordanoLanzafame2005_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GiordanoLanzafame2005-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_total_primary_energy_consumption_and_production" title="List of countries by total primary energy consumption and production">tenth largest</a> energy consumer with much of its energy coming from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable sources</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a> is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric plant</a> by energy generation.<sup id="cite_ref-SchmidtOnyango2011_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchmidtOnyango2011-233">[233]</a></sup> The first car with an ethanol engine was produced in 1978 and the first airplane engine running on ethanol in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-OECDDevelopment2001_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECDDevelopment2001-234">[234]</a></sup> Recent oil discoveries in the <a href="/wiki/Pre-salt_layer" title="Pre-salt layer">Pre-salt layer</a> have opened the door for a large increase in oil production.<sup id="cite_ref-BrainardMartinez-Diaz2009_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BrainardMartinez-Diaz2009-235">[235]</a></sup> The governmental agencies responsible for the energy policy are the Ministry of Mines and Energy, the National Council for Energy Policy, the <a href="/wiki/National_Agency_of_Petroleum,_Natural_Gas_and_Biofuels_(Brazil)" title="National Agency of Petroleum, Natural Gas and Biofuels (Brazil)">National Agency of Petroleum, Natural Gas and Biofuels</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Electricity_Regulatory_Agency" title="Brazilian Electricity Regulatory Agency">National Agency of Electricity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD2005_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD2005-236">[236]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1108px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg" class="image" title="The Itaipu Dam on the Paraná River, located on the border between Brazil and Paraguay, is the second largest of the world (the first is the Three Gorges Dam, in China). Approximately 75% of the Brazilian energy matrix, one of the cleanest in the world, comes from hydropower."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg/1100px-Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg" width="1100" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg/1650px-Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg/2200px-Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4016" data-file-height="651" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Itaipu_%C3%A0_noite.jpg" title="File:Itaipu à noite.jpg"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">Paraná River</a>, located on the border between Brazil and Paraguay, is the second largest of the world (the first is the <a href="/wiki/Three_Gorges_Dam" title="Three Gorges Dam">Three Gorges Dam</a>, in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>). Approximately 75% of the <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_Brazil" title="Energy policy of Brazil">Brazilian energy matrix</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/Clean_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Clean energy">cleanest</a> in the world, comes from <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Brazil" title="Tourism in Brazil">Tourism in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Noronha_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Noronha_02.jpg/220px-Noronha_02.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Noronha_02.jpg/330px-Noronha_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Noronha_02.jpg/440px-Noronha_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3459" data-file-height="1946" /></a>
