<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oca_do_Brasil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Oca_(structure)" title="Oca (structure)">Oca</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kamayur%C3%A1_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kamayurá people">Kamayurá people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xingu_Indigenous_Park" title="Xingu Indigenous Park">Xingu Indigenous Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso" title="Mato Grosso">Mato Grosso</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The official language of Brazil is Portuguese<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_People_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_People-356">[356]</a></sup> (Article 13 of the Constitution of the Federal Republic of Brazil), which almost all of the population speaks and is virtually the only language used in newspapers, radio, television, and for business and administrative purposes. The most famous exception to this is a strong <a href="/wiki/Recognition_of_sign_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Recognition of sign languages">sign language law</a> that was passed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress of Brazil</a>. Legally recognized in 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-Libras_2002_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Libras_2002-357">[357]</a></sup> the law was <a href="/wiki/Regulation" title="Regulation">regulated</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Libras_2005_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Libras_2005-358">[358]</a></sup> The law mandates the use of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Sign_Language" title="Brazilian Sign Language">Brazilian Sign Language</a>, more commonly known by its Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronym</a> LIBRAS, in education and government services. The language must be taught as a part of the <a href="/wiki/School_of_education" title="School of education">education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Speech_and_language_pathology" class="mw-redirect" title="Speech and language pathology">speech and language pathology</a> curricula. LIBRAS teachers, instructors and translators are recognized professionals. Schools and health services must provide access ("<a href="/wiki/Inclusion_(education)" title="Inclusion (education)">inclusion</a>") to <a href="/wiki/Deaf_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Deaf community">deaf people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Russo2011_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russo2011-359">[359]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">Brazilian Portuguese</a> has had its own development, mostly similar to 16th-century Central and Southern dialects of European Portuguese<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[360]</a></sup> (despite a very substantial number of Portuguese colonial settlers, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Brazilian">more recent immigrants</a>, coming from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Portugal">Northern regions</a>, and in minor degree Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a>), with a few influences from the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Amerindian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African languages</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> restricted to the vocabulary only.<sup id="cite_ref-Portuguese_361-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portuguese-361">[361]</a></sup> As a result,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> the language is somewhat different, mostly in phonology, from the language of Portugal and other <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese-speaking countries">Portuguese-speaking countries</a> (the dialects of the other countries, partly because of the more recent end of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese colonialism</a> in these regions, have a closer connection to contemporary <a href="/wiki/European_Portuguese" title="European Portuguese">European Portuguese</a>). These differences are comparable to those between <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Portuguese_361-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portuguese-361">[361]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil is the only Portuguese-speaking nation in the Americas, making the language an important part of Brazilian national identity and giving it a national culture distinct from those of its Spanish-speaking neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-language2_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-language2-362">[362]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg/220px-Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg/330px-Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg/440px-Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="3216" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portal_de_Pomerode.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pomerode" title="Pomerode">Pomerode</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a>, is one of the municipalities with a cooficial language. In this region, <a href="/wiki/Hunsr%C3%BCckisch_dialect" title="Hunsrückisch dialect">Hunsrückisch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pomeranian_language" title="Pomeranian language">Pomeranian</a>, German dialects, are two of the minor languages (see <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_German" title="Brazilian German">Brazilian German</a>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1990, the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP), which included representatives from all countries with Portuguese as the official language, reached an <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Language_Orthographic_Agreement_of_1990" title="Portuguese Language Orthographic Agreement of 1990">agreement on the reform of the Portuguese orthography</a> to unify the two standards then in use by Brazil on one side and the remaining lusophone countries on the other. This spelling reform went into effect in Brazil on 1 January 2009. In Portugal, the reform was signed into law by the President on 21 July 2008 allowing for a 6-year adaptation period, during which both orthographies will co-exist. The remaining CPLP countries are free to establish their own transition timetables.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup></p>
<p>Minority languages are spoken throughout the nation. One hundred and eighty <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Amerindian languages</a> are spoken in remote areas and a significant number of other languages are spoken by immigrants and their descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-Portuguese_361-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portuguese-361">[361]</a></sup> In the municipality of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Gabriel_da_Cachoeira" title="São Gabriel da Cachoeira">São Gabriel da Cachoeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nheengatu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nheengatu language">Nheengatu</a> (a currently endangered South American <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole language</a> – or an 'anti-creole', according to some linguists – with mostly Indigenous Brazilian languages lexicon and Portuguese-based grammar that, together with its southern relative <a href="/wiki/L%C3%ADngua_geral_paulista" class="mw-redirect" title="Língua geral paulista">língua geral paulista</a>, once was a major <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> in Brazil<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, being replaced by Portuguese only after governmental prohibition led by <a href="/wiki/Suppression_of_the_Society_of_Jesus#Portugal" title="Suppression of the Society of Jesus">major political changes</a>)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Opinion" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:TERSE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:TERSE"><span title="Statements that may be excessive (July 2015)">excessive detail?</span></a></i>]</sup>, <a href="/wiki/Baniwa_language" title="Baniwa language">Baniwa</a> and Tucano languages had been granted co-official status with Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-language_364-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-language-364">[364]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are significant communities of German (mostly the <a href="/wiki/Riograndenser_Hunsr%C3%BCckisch" class="mw-redirect" title="Riograndenser Hunsrückisch">Brazilian Hunsrückisch</a>, a High German language dialect) and Italian (mostly the <a href="/wiki/Talian_dialect" title="Talian dialect">Talian</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a> dialect) origins in the Southern and Southeastern regions, whose ancestors' native languages were carried along to Brazil, and which, still alive there, are influenced by the Portuguese language.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup> Talian is officially a historic patrimony of <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup> and two German dialects possess co-official status in a few municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-Stevenson1997_368-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stevenson1997-368">[368]</a></sup></p>
<p>Learning at least one second language (generally English or Spanish) is mandatory for all the 12 grades of the mandatory <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Brazil" title="Education in Brazil">education system</a> (<a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary education</a>, there called <i>ensino fundamental</i> and <i>ensino médio</i> respectively). Brazil is the first country in South America to offer <a href="/wiki/Esperanto" title="Esperanto">Esperanto</a> to secondary students.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg/220px-Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg/330px-Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg/440px-Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2948" data-file-height="1965" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salvador-SFranciscoChurch2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Interior of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Francisco_Church_and_Convent" title="São Francisco Church and Convent">São Francisco Church and Convent</a> in <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador, Bahia</a>, one of the richest expressions of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_in_Brazil" title="Baroque in Brazil">Brazilian baroque</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brazil" title="Culture of Brazil">Culture of Brazil</a></div>
<p>The core culture of Brazil is derived from <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portuguese culture</a>, because of its strong colonial ties with the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Meade2009_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meade2009-370">[370]</a></sup> Among other influences, the Portuguese introduced the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manueline" title="Manueline">colonial architectural styles</a>. The culture was, however, also strongly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">indigenous</a> and non-Portuguese European cultures and traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinson1998_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinson1998-371">[371]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some aspects of Brazilian culture were influenced by the contributions of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Brazilian">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="German Brazilian">German</a> and other European as well <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Brazilian">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Brazilian">Jewish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab Brazilian">Arab</a> immigrants who arrived in large numbers in the South and Southeast of Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-Lesser2013a_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lesser2013a-372">[372]</a></sup> The indigenous Amerindians influenced Brazil's language and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_cuisine" title="Brazilian cuisine">cuisine</a>; and the Africans influenced language, cuisine, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Brazil" title="Music of Brazil">music</a>, dance and religion.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brazilian_art" title="Brazilian art">Brazilian art</a> has developed since the 16th century into different styles that range from <a href="/wiki/Baroque_in_Brazil" title="Baroque in Brazil">Baroque</a> (the dominant style in Brazil until the early 19th century)<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-itaucultural.org.br_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itaucultural.org.br-375">[375]</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_academic_art" title="Brazilian academic art">Romanticism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">Modernism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressionism" title="Expressionism">Expressionism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">Cubism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">Surrealism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abstract_art" title="Abstract art">Abstractionism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Brazil" title="Cinema of Brazil">Brazilian cinema</a> dates back to the birth of the medium in the late 19th century and has gained a new level of international acclaim since the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-Marsh2012_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marsh2012-376">[376]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Brazil" title="Music of Brazil">Music of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:358px;max-width:358px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Heitor_Vila-Lobos_(c._1922)part.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Heitor_Vila-Lobos_%28c._1922%29part.jpg/120px-Heitor_Vila-Lobos_%28c._1922%29part.jpg" width="120" height="175" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Heitor_Vila-Lobos_%28c._1922%29part.jpg/180px-Heitor_Vila-Lobos_%28c._1922%29part.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4b/Heitor_Vila-Lobos_%28c._1922%29part.jpg 2x" data-file-width="219" data-file-height="320" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Heitor_Villa-Lobos" title="Heitor Villa-Lobos">Heitor Villa-Lobos</a>, one of the great Latin composers</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:232px;max-width:232px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos_Tom_Jobim_cigar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f8/Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos_Tom_Jobim_cigar.jpg/230px-Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos_Tom_Jobim_cigar.jpg" width="230" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f8/Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos_Tom_Jobim_cigar.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="240" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Tom_Jobim" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Jobim">Tom Jobim</a>, one of the leading names of <a href="/wiki/Bossa_nova" title="Bossa nova">bossa nova</a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The music of Brazil was formed mainly from the fusion of European and African elements.<sup id="cite_ref-FonsecaWeiner1991_377-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FonsecaWeiner1991-377">[377]</a></sup> Until the nineteenth century, Portugal was the gateway to most of the influences that built Brazilian music, although many of these elements were not of Portuguese origin, but generally European. The first was José Maurício Nunes Garcia, author of sacred pieces with influence of Viennese classicism.<sup id="cite_ref-Grazia2013_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grazia2013-378">[378]</a></sup> The major contribution of the African element was the rhythmic diversity and some dances and instruments that had a bigger role in the development of popular music and folk, flourishing especially in the twentieth century.<sup id="cite_ref-FonsecaWeiner1991_377-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FonsecaWeiner1991-377">[377]</a></sup></p>
<p>Popular music since the late eighteenth century began to show signs of forming a characteristically Brazilian sound, with <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">samba</a> considered the most typical and on the UNESCO cultural heritage list.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maracatu" title="Maracatu">Maracatu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afox%C3%AA" title="Afoxê">Afoxê</a> are two <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Brazilian">Afro-Brazilian</a> music traditions that have been popularized by their appearance in the annual <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Carnival" title="Brazilian Carnival">Brazilian Carnivals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Crook2009_380-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crook2009-380">[380]</a></sup> The sport of <a href="/wiki/Capoeira" title="Capoeira">capoeira</a> is usually played with its own music referred to as <a href="/wiki/Capoeira_music" title="Capoeira music">capoeira music</a>, which is usually considered to be a call-and-response type of folk music.<sup id="cite_ref-Fryer2000_381-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fryer2000-381">[381]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Choro" title="Choro">Choro</a> is a very popular music instrumental style. Its origins are in 19th-century Rio de Janeiro. In spite of the name, the style often has a fast and happy rhythm, characterized by virtuosity, improvisation, subtle <a href="/wiki/Modulation_(music)" title="Modulation (music)">modulations</a> and full of <a href="/wiki/Syncopation" title="Syncopation">syncopation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counterpoint" title="Counterpoint">counterpoint</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MacGowanPessanha1998_382-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacGowanPessanha1998-382">[382]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bossa_nova" title="Bossa nova">Bossa nova</a> is also a well-known style of Brazilian music developed and popularized in the 1950s and 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-MacGowanPessanha1998b_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacGowanPessanha1998b-383">[383]</a></sup> The phrase "bossa nova" means literally "new trend".<sup id="cite_ref-Kassing2007_384-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kassing2007-384">[384]</a></sup> A lyrical fusion of samba and <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, bossa nova acquired a large following starting in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-Campbell2011b_385-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell2011b-385">[385]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1208px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg" class="image" title="The Rio Carnival, a type of samba parade."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg/1200px-Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg" width="1200" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg/1800px-Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg/2400px-Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="360" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sapucai_Panoramic.jpg" title="File:Sapucai Panoramic.jpg"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Rio_Carnival" title="Rio Carnival">Rio Carnival</a>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">samba</a> parade.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg/170px-Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg" width="170" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg/255px-Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg/340px-Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1263" data-file-height="1852" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Machado_de_Assis_aos_57_anos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Machado_de_Assis" title="Machado de Assis">Machado de Assis</a>, poet and novelist, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Academia_Brasileira_de_Letras" title="Academia Brasileira de Letras">Brazilian Academy of Letters</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_literature" title="Brazilian literature">Brazilian literature</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brazilian_literature" title="Brazilian literature">Brazilian literature</a> dates back to the 16th century, to the writings of the first Portuguese explorers in Brazil, such as <a href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_Vaz_de_Caminha" title="Pêro Vaz de Caminha">Pêro Vaz de Caminha</a>, filled with descriptions of <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">fauna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> and commentary about the indigenous population that fascinated European readers.<sup id="cite_ref-CrocittiVallance2012_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrocittiVallance2012-386">[386]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil produced significant works in <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romanticism</a> – novelists like <a href="/wiki/Joaquim_Manuel_de_Macedo" title="Joaquim Manuel de Macedo">Joaquim Manuel de Macedo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Alencar" title="José de Alencar">José de Alencar</a> wrote novels about love and pain. Alencar, in his long career, also treated indigenous people as heroes in the <a href="/wiki/Indianism_(arts)" title="Indianism (arts)">Indigenist</a> novels <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guarani" title="The Guarani">O Guarani</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Iracema" title="Iracema">Iracema</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ubirajara" class="mw-redirect" title="Ubirajara">Ubirajara</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[387]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Machado_de_Assis" title="Machado de Assis">Machado de Assis</a>, one of his contemporaries, wrote in virtually all genres and continues to gain international prestige from critics worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[389]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[390]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_literature#Modernism" title="Brazilian literature">Brazilian Modernism</a>, evidenced by the <a href="/wiki/Week_of_Modern_Art" class="mw-redirect" title="Week of Modern Art">Week of Modern Art</a> in 1922, was concerned with a nationalist avant-garde literature,<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[391]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_literature#Post-Modernism" title="Brazilian literature">Post-Modernism</a> brought a generation of distinct poets like <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Cabral_de_Melo_Neto" title="João Cabral de Melo Neto">João Cabral de Melo Neto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Drummond_de_Andrade" title="Carlos Drummond de Andrade">Carlos Drummond de Andrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinicius_de_Moraes" title="Vinicius de Moraes">Vinicius de Moraes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cora_Coralina" title="Cora Coralina">Cora Coralina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graciliano_Ramos" title="Graciliano Ramos">Graciliano Ramos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cec%C3%ADlia_Meireles" title="Cecília Meireles">Cecília Meireles</a>, and internationally known writers dealing with universal and regional subjects like <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Amado" title="Jorge Amado">Jorge Amado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Guimar%C3%A3es_Rosa" title="João Guimarães Rosa">João Guimarães Rosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarice_Lispector" title="Clarice Lispector">Clarice Lispector</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Bandeira" title="Manuel Bandeira">Manuel Bandeira</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">[392]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[393]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">[394]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_cuisine" title="Brazilian cuisine">Brazilian cuisine</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brazilian_dishes" title="List of Brazilian dishes">List of Brazilian dishes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:415px;max-width:415px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:209px;max-width:209px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Brigadeiro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Brigadeiro.jpg/207px-Brigadeiro.jpg" width="207" height="155" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Brigadeiro.jpg/311px-Brigadeiro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Brigadeiro.jpg/414px-Brigadeiro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Brigadeiro" title="Brigadeiro">Brigadeiro</a> is a national candy and one most and is recognized as one of the main dishes of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_cuisine" title="Brazilian cuisine">Brazilian cuisine</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Feijoada_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Feijoada_01.jpg/200px-Feijoada_01.jpg" width="200" height="157" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Feijoada_01.jpg/300px-Feijoada_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/Feijoada_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="342" data-file-height="268" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Feijoada" title="Feijoada">Feijoada</a> is a typical Brazilian dish</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brazilian cuisine varies greatly by region, reflecting the country's varying mix of indigenous and immigrant populations. This has created a national cuisine marked by the preservation of regional differences.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_4_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta_4-395">[395]</a></sup> Examples are <a href="/wiki/Feijoada" title="Feijoada">Feijoada</a>, considered the country's national dish;<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">[396]</a></sup> and regional foods such as <a href="/wiki/Vatap%C3%A1" title="Vatapá">vatapá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moqueca" title="Moqueca">moqueca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">polenta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acaraj%C3%A9" title="Acarajé">acarajé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">[397]</a></sup></p>
<p>The national beverage is <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cacha%C3%A7a" title="Cachaça">cachaça</a> is Brazil's native <a href="/wiki/Distilled_beverage" title="Distilled beverage">liquor</a>. Cachaça is distilled from <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugar cane</a> and is the main ingredient in the national cocktail, <a href="/wiki/Caipirinha" title="Caipirinha">Caipirinha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bayor2011_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bayor2011-398">[398]</a></sup></p>
<p>A typical meal consists mostly of <a href="/wiki/Rice_and_beans" title="Rice and beans">rice and beans</a> with <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salad</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">french fries</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Fried_egg" title="Fried egg">fried egg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">[399]</a></sup> Often, it's mixed with cassava flour (<a href="/wiki/Farofa" title="Farofa">farofa</a>). Fried potatoes, fried cassava, fried banana, fried meat and fried cheese are very often eaten in lunch and served in most typical restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">[400]</a></sup> Popular snacks are <a href="/wiki/Pastel_(food)" title="Pastel (food)">pastel</a> (a fired pastry); <a href="/wiki/Coxinha" title="Coxinha">coxinha</a> (a variation of chicken croquete); <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A3o_de_queijo" title="Pão de queijo">pão de queijo</a> (cheese bread and cassava flour / <a href="/wiki/Tapioca" title="Tapioca">tapioca</a>); <a href="/wiki/Pamonha" title="Pamonha">pamonha</a> (corn and milk paste); <a href="/wiki/Sfiha" title="Sfiha">esfirra</a> (A variation of Lebanese pastry); <a href="/wiki/Kibbeh" title="Kibbeh">kibbeh</a> (from Arabic cuisine); <a href="/wiki/Empanada" title="Empanada">empanada</a> (pastry) and <a href="/wiki/Empada" class="mw-redirect" title="Empada">empada</a>, little salt pies filled with shrimps or heart of palm.</p>
<p>Brazil has a variety of candies such as <a href="/wiki/Brigadeiro" title="Brigadeiro">brigadeiros</a> (chocolate fudge balls), <a href="/wiki/Cocada" class="mw-redirect" title="Cocada">cocada</a> (a coconut sweet), <a href="/wiki/Beijinho" title="Beijinho">beijinhos</a> (coconut truffles and clove) and romeu e julieta (cheese with a guava jam known as <a href="/wiki/Goiabada" title="Goiabada">goiabada</a>). Peanuts are used to make <a href="/wiki/Pa%C3%A7oca" title="Paçoca">paçoca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rapadura" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapadura">rapadura</a> and <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9-de-moleque" title="Pé-de-moleque">pé-de-moleque</a>. Local common fruits like <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A7a%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Açaí">açaí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cupua%C3%A7u" title="Cupuaçu">cupuaçu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cashew" title="Cashew">cashew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guava" title="Guava">guava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">orange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">lime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Passionfruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Passionfruit">passionfruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapple</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spondias" title="Spondias">hog plum</a> are turned in <a href="/wiki/Juice" title="Juice">juices</a> and used to make <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Popsicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Popsicle">popsicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream">ice cream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">[401]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_festivais.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Palacio_festivais.jpg/220px-Palacio_festivais.jpg" width="220" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Palacio_festivais.jpg/330px-Palacio_festivais.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Palacio_festivais.jpg/440px-Palacio_festivais.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Festival_de_Gramado" title="Festival de Gramado">Gramado Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Fernando_Meirelles_-_%C3%96sterreichpremiere_360_Wiener_Volkstheater_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Fernando_Meirelles_-_%C3%96sterreichpremiere_360_Wiener_Volkstheater_01.jpg/220px-Fernando_Meirelles_-_%C3%96sterreichpremiere_360_Wiener_Volkstheater_01.jpg" width="220" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Fernando_Meirelles_-_%C3%96sterreichpremiere_360_Wiener_Volkstheater_01.jpg/330px-Fernando_Meirelles_-_%C3%96sterreichpremiere_360_Wiener_Volkstheater_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Fernando_Meirelles_-_%C3%96sterreichpremiere_360_Wiener_Volkstheater_01.jpg/440px-Fernando_Meirelles_-_%C3%96sterreichpremiere_360_Wiener_Volkstheater_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1094" data-file-height="729" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Fernando_Meirelles" title="Fernando Meirelles">Fernando Meirelles</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Brazil" title="Cinema of Brazil">Cinema of Brazil</a></div>
<p>The Brazilian film industry began in the late 19th century, during the early days of the <a href="/wiki/Belle_%C3%89poque" title="Belle Époque">Belle Époque</a>. While there were national film productions during the early 20th century, American films such as <i>Rio the Magnificent</i> were made in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> to promote tourism in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">[402]</a></sup> The films <i><a href="/wiki/Limite" class="mw-redirect" title="Limite">Limite</a></i> (1931) and <i><a href="/wiki/Ganga_Bruta" title="Ganga Bruta">Ganga Bruta</a></i> (1933), the latter being produced by <a href="/wiki/Adhemar_Gonzaga" title="Adhemar Gonzaga">Adhemar Gonzaga</a> through the prolific studio Cinédia, were poorly received at release and failed at the box office, but are acclaimed nowadays and placed among the finest Brazilian films of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">[403]</a></sup> The 1941 unfinished film <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_All_True_(film)" title="It's All True (film)">It's All True</a></i> was divided in four segments, two of which were filmed in Brazil and directed by <a href="/wiki/Orson_Welles" title="Orson Welles">Orson Welles</a>; it was originally produced as part of the United States' <a href="/wiki/Good_Neighbor_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Good Neighbor Policy">Good Neighbor Policy</a> during Getúlio Vargas' Estado Novo government.</p>
<p>During the 1960s the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_Novo" title="Cinema Novo">Cinema Novo</a> movement rose to prominence with directors such as <a href="/wiki/Glauber_Rocha" title="Glauber Rocha">Glauber Rocha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Pereira_dos_Santos" title="Nelson Pereira dos Santos">Nelson Pereira dos Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Cesar_Saraceni" class="mw-redirect" title="Paulo Cesar Saraceni">Paulo Cesar Saraceni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arnaldo_Jabor" title="Arnaldo Jabor">Arnaldo Jabor</a>. Rocha's films <i><a href="/wiki/Deus_e_o_Diabo_na_Terra_do_Sol" class="mw-redirect" title="Deus e o Diabo na Terra do Sol">Deus e o Diabo na Terra do Sol</a></i> (1964) and <i><a href="/wiki/Terra_em_Transe" class="mw-redirect" title="Terra em Transe">Terra em Transe</a></i> (1967) are considered to be some of the greatest and most influential in Brazilian film history.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">[404]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1990s Brazil saw a surge of critical and commercial success with films such as <i><a href="/wiki/O_Quatrilho" title="O Quatrilho">O Quatrilho</a></i> (1995), <i><a href="/wiki/O_Que_%C3%89_Isso,_Companheiro%3F" class="mw-redirect" title="O Que É Isso, Companheiro?">O Que É Isso, Companheiro?</a></i> (1997) and <i><a href="/wiki/Central_do_Brasil" title="Central do Brasil">Central do Brasil</a></i> (1998), all of which were nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" title="Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film">Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film</a>, the latter receiving a <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Fernanda_Montenegro" title="Fernanda Montenegro">Fernanda Montenegro</a>. The 2002 crime film <i><a href="/wiki/City_of_God_(2002_film)" title="City of God (2002 film)">City of God</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Meirelles" title="Fernando Meirelles">Fernando Meirelles</a>, was critically acclaimed, scoring 90% on <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">[405]</a></sup> being placed in <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a>'s Best Films of the Decade list<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">[406]</a></sup> and receiving four <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominations in 2004, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Best Director</a>. Notable film festivals in Brazil include the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_International_Film_Festival" title="São Paulo International Film Festival">São Paulo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_International_Film_Festival" title="Rio de Janeiro International Film Festival">Rio de Janeiro International Film Festivals</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Festival_de_Gramado" title="Festival de Gramado">Gramado Festival</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Selo_da_Copa_de_1970_3_cruzeiros.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Selo_da_Copa_de_1970_3_cruzeiros.jpg/220px-Selo_da_Copa_de_1970_3_cruzeiros.jpg" width="220" height="149" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Selo_da_Copa_de_1970_3_cruzeiros.jpg/330px-Selo_da_Copa_de_1970_3_cruzeiros.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Selo_da_Copa_de_1970_3_cruzeiros.jpg/440px-Selo_da_Copa_de_1970_3_cruzeiros.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2714" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Stamp for the victory of the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian team</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970 FIFA World Cup</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Ayrton_Senna_with_toy_car_cropped_no_wm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ayrton_Senna_with_toy_car_cropped_no_wm.jpg/220px-Ayrton_Senna_with_toy_car_cropped_no_wm.jpg" width="220" height="151" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ayrton_Senna_with_toy_car_cropped_no_wm.jpg/330px-Ayrton_Senna_with_toy_car_cropped_no_wm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ayrton_Senna_with_toy_car_cropped_no_wm.jpg/440px-Ayrton_Senna_with_toy_car_cropped_no_wm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1197" data-file-height="821" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">Senna</a>, one of the biggest names in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">F1</a>'s history.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Brazil" title="Sport in Brazil">Sport in Brazil</a></div>
<p>The most popular sport in Brazil is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">[407]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian men's national team</a> is ranked among the best in the world according to the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>, and has won the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> tournament a record five times.<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">[408]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">[409]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auto_racing" title="Auto racing">auto racing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">martial arts</a> also attract large audiences. The <a href="/wiki/Brazil_men%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Brazil men's national volleyball team">Brazil men's national volleyball team</a>, for example, currently holds the titles of the <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_World_League" title="FIVB Volleyball World League">World League</a>, <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_World_Grand_Champions_Cup" title="FIVB Volleyball World Grand Champions Cup">World Grand Champions Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship">World Championship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Cup" title="FIVB Volleyball Men's World Cup">World Cup</a>.</p>
<p>Some sport variations have their origins in Brazil: <a href="/wiki/Beach_soccer" title="Beach soccer">beach football</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">[410]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> (indoor football)<sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-411">[411]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Footvolley" title="Footvolley">footvolley</a> emerged in Brazil as variations of football. In martial arts, Brazilians developed <a href="/wiki/Capoeira" title="Capoeira">Capoeira</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">[412]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vale_tudo" title="Vale tudo">Vale tudo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">[413]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Jiu-Jitsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu">Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">[414]</a></sup></p>
<p>In auto racing, three Brazilian drivers have won the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> world championship eight times.<sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">[415]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-416" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-416">[416]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">[417]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brazil has hosted several high-profile international sporting events, like the <a href="/wiki/1950_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1950 FIFA World Cup">1950 FIFA World Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-418" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-418">[418]</a></sup> and recently has hosted the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">[419]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> circuit, <a href="/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace" title="Autódromo José Carlos Pace">Autódromo José Carlos Pace</a>, hosts the annual <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="Brazilian Grand Prix">Grand Prix of Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-420">[420]</a></sup></p>
<p>São Paulo organized the <a href="/wiki/1963_Pan_American_Games" title="1963 Pan American Games">IV Pan American Games</a> in 1963, and Rio de Janeiro hosted the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">XV Pan American Games</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-LiMacIntosh2011_421-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LiMacIntosh2011-421">[421]</a></sup> On 2 October 2009, Rio de Janeiro was selected to host the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Olympic Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Paralympics" title="2016 Summer Paralympics">2016 Paralympic Games</a>, making it the first South American city to host the games<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_olympics_422-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_olympics-422">[422]</a></sup> and second in Latin America after <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>. Furthermore, the country hosted the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Basketball_World_Cup" title="FIBA Basketball World Cup">FIBA Basketball World Cups</a> in <a href="/wiki/1954_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1954 FIBA World Championship">1954</a> and <a href="/wiki/1963_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1963 FIBA World Championship">1963</a>. At the 1963 event, the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_basketball_team" title="Brazil national basketball team">Brazil national basketball team</a> won one of its two world championship titles.<sup id="cite_ref-FIBA_History_423-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIBA_History-423">[423]</a></sup></p>

<div style="padding:0px;"><b><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Lat. <small>and</small> Long.</a> <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Brazil&amp;params=15_45_S_47_57_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">15°45′S</span> <span class="longitude">47°57′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">15.750°S 47.950°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">-15.750; -47.950</span></span></span></a></span> <span style="color:darkblue">(Brasilia)</span></b>

<tr>
<th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="font-weight:normal;">Entire</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
